# Real World Gis

> Geographic information systems, or GIS, is a way to approach mapping and spacial analysis using a computer environment. Learning GIS requires training in cartography, database management, and spatial analysis. But once you've built a solid foundation in the basics, how do you approach GIS challenges in the real world? In this course, Dr. Jason VanHorn helps you master practical, real-world GIS sce

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766) | Intermediate | 60K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

#### Where is the GIS data?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Today, we are inundated with data.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980&t=3)** On our phones, televisions, and computers, we've become a data-driven society.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980&t=9)** Spatial geographic data are everywhere, yet the top question I get from students is where is the GIS data?
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980&t=17)** In this chapter of real world GIS, I will introduce the topic of GIS data trends and introduce you to five GIS data locations to give you the knowledge of where to get GIS data, but also to equip you with tools to master the download aspects of GIS data portals that should be replicable on almost any GIS data portal site.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-is-the-gis-data?u=76281980&t=40)** So let's get started with some trends.

#### How to consider the scale of GIS data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] GIS data come in different data forms.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=3)** But one thing consistent with all GIS data is scale.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=8)** So you have to ask yourself what scale do you want your GIS data?
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=13)** Do you need it at a global or a national scale or more close to home like a regional or local scale?
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=21)** Answering that question will help you decide where to download your data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=27)** Global or national level data compare country to country, typically one statistic is calculated for each country and so we know how the country is doing based on some category.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=40)** For example, here I've mapped child under nourishment by country all around the world from the World Bank dataset.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=49)** Now this map is showing the most recently reported data for countries who have provided their data since 2010.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=58)** And we can use this kind of map to compare and contrast each country that we have data for.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=65)** Subnational GIS data drills down inside a country to give us data at a more regional scale.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=73)** In the United States that would be state level data, which allow us to compare between states on some category.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=81)** Here I've mapped by US state the percentage of people that have engaged with YouTube in the last 30 days.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=90)** The easiest way I found to get national data is from country statistical offices like a census bureau or a national statistics office.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=101)** So if you need that kind of data, do online searches first for those places in the country of your choice.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=109)** Now the other form of subnational data is much more local.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=113)** We can drill down even further within a region or a state to get more local knowledge.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=119)** Here, I've created the same data set of the percentage of people who have watched YouTube in the last month by county in my state of Michigan.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=130)** And here is the same subnational GIS data but even more local within a city.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=136)** So what scale do you want for GIS data?
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=140)** Do you need GIS data covering a global or a national level, or do you need it at a regional or a local scale?
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-consider-the-scale-of-gis-data?u=76281980&t=148)** So considering this question will help you quickly determine where you will look for your GIS data needs.

#### What spatial data are already in ArcGIS?

>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=10)** And that's what I'm showing you here.

>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=23)** And so you'll use this most often in your workflows and in your projects that you do daily.

>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=249)** There is one additional data product that I'd like to mention that's available inside of ArcGIS Pro.

>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=262)** It's an extension within ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=265)** And you can find that under the analysis and business analysis tab.
>

>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=279)** You can find business facility locations or you can find a whole host of different kinds of data, population, business, education, et cetera.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-spatial-data-are-already-in-arcgis?u=76281980&t=289)** So if you have this extension, it can be very very helpful for your daily workflows.

#### How to get census GIS data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So we need census GIS data.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=3)** Now, most countries have a national census by law, and here in the United States, we have a census every 10 years since 1790.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=12)** Census bureaus today have an almost embarrassment of data richness, so it's very easy to get overwhelmed by the amount of data on these sites.

> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=183)** Now, in this webpage, we can see on the left, we have different filters, and in this case, we're going to filter by the geographic level we're interested in.

> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=192)** In the middle are the tables, and we also have a preview of the table on the right.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=198)** So let's go ahead and filter by those block groups.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=201)** I will choose Geography and then block group, and here, I will choose the state that I'm interested in, Michigan, and now I will choose All Block Groups within Michigan.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=213)** Now that I've set that filter, all of the data that I try and find in this web interface will be filtered based on that level of geography.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=224)** So now I'll click on All, and now I will choose whatever kind of table data that I'm interested.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=229)** I could do a search, or in this case, let's use this for the example, P1 level data, which is total population by the geography we're interested in.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=240)** To download this data, I simply click on Download Table Data at the top of the column.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=245)** I choose the thing that I want, in this case, P1, and then I click on Download.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=251)** Now I have to confirm what level I want since there are multiple data products linked to P1.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=257)** In this case, I can't get the 2020 census, but I can get the 2010 census, so I will select that for the Summary File, which is what I want.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=267)** Now I'll click on the DOWNLOAD.CSV and download it.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=272)** Great, so now we've collected the geographic file and the data file, and that's how you download data from the Census Bureau.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-get-census-gis-data?u=76281980&t=280)** Now we can unzip those files and do a join within ArcGIS Pro, and we can then use those files to visualize our geographic entities, in this case, total population by block group in the state of Michigan.

### 2. What Can Be Done with GIS Data?

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Understanding GIS data types
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] GIS data typically tries to represent reality.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=4)** The re-presentation or representation of places as points or polygons or images acts as a metaphor for reality, and as the mapmaker or cartographer, you have the variety of symbology available to you in ArcMap and ArcGIS Pro to visualize and enable design options for your data.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=24)** There are two main GIS data types.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=27)** Vector data refers mostly to data represented as points or lines or polygons, while raster data is made up of rows and columns or grids and pixels and is most commonly thought of as imagery.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=43)** I'll discuss both later in this course.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=46)** The data types have developed since the advent of the 1960s emergence of GIS in Canada, in England, and the United States, and through the work of several people in analytical cartography, vector data and raster data types became the dominant vocabulary.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=64)** With the advent of the personal computer in the 1980s, ESRI focus was on software application development of ArcInfo.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=73)** According to the ESRI website, they first developed ArcInfo in 1982 for microcomputers, and by 1986, a PC version was available and distributed.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=85)** ArcInfo is a command-line based software package that handles both vector and raster geographic data, and it's been the industry standard tool since its implementation, even though other competitors do exist.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=98)** In contrast to ArcInfo, a much less exhaustive ESRI software package called ArcView was released in the early 1990s.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=107)** Although not as comprehensive as ArcInfo, ArcView has a major advantage over its big brother, a graphical user interface.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=115)** It's with this graphical user interface that ArcView has become one of the most popular GIS packages worldwide.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=124)** In late 1999, ArcView 8 was released, which is better known under its new name, ArcGIS, which is an umbrella term for all the components of ArcGIS.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=136)** ESRI combined many of the features of ArcInfo into a redesigned graphical user interface to produce an all-in-one GIS system.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=145)** We call our current software ArcView 10.8 or ArcGIS 10.8, and some just call it ArcMap 10.8.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=155)** ArcGIS Pro was released in 2015.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=159)** It is a powerful and complex GIS software.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=163)** Built on the concepts and experience of ArcView, ArcGIS Pro takes advantage of current computing technology.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=172)** It is 64-bit enabled and has 2D and 3D mapping capabilities, and is tightly coupled to the the [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) online environment, tapping into the wider ESRI software ecosystem.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/understanding-gis-data-types?u=76281980&t=185)** ESRI has introduced different vector data models with ArcInfo, ArcView, and ArcGIS while expanding data options for raster data, so let's dive into those now.

#### Mastering vector GIS data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Esri has released two vector data models for GIS users, let's go through each.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=6)** So you are a master of vector GIS data.

> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=10)** Vector GIS data in ArcGIS and ArcGIS Pro is either in the georelational or the geodatabase model.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=18)** The georelational vector data model is structured with a separate file system of associated files and is non-object-oriented.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=27)** Common georelational files are coverages and shapefiles.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=32)** Now the second model is the geodatabase model which has a contained file system and is object oriented and most readily associated with the geodatabase file.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=43)** You will find both of these vector data structures are widely present in the available data that you can download.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=51)** The coverage vector data model was introduced with Arcinfo and just like the software sounds, arc describes geometry objects like points, lines and polygons, whereas info describes attribute information about the arcs.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=66)** If coverage data has points of cities we might see those points on a map and then be able to query any of their attributes.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=74)** The coverage data model contains the point information of the location and the attribute information of the relation to the point.

> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=251)** Introduced in ArcView 8 or ArcGIS 8, the geodatabase model is a contained file system and a true relational database with all the advantages associated with database management.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=264)** Instead of a flat file system, the geodatabase stores the geography as objects.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=269)** So you can apply structured query language or SQL functions and operators on the geodatabase.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=277)** Esri's first model started with the personal geodatabase which was based on the Microsoft Jet database engine.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=284)** The personal geodatabase has a two gigabyte storage limit.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=288)** It is being phased out by Microsoft and its not an option in ArcGIS Pro, which leaves us with the wonderful file geodatabase, and exclusive to ArcGIS Pro, the mobile geodatabase.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=302)** The geodatabase vocabulary is simple, geodatabases have two main aspects, feature data sets and feature classes.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=310)** Feature sets house a series of feature classes that share the same geographic projection.

> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=317)** I'll cover projections elsewhere in this course.

>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=326)** There is no limit to the number of feature classes that you can have within a geodatabase, as a standalone or within a feature dataset.

> **[9:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-vector-gis-data?u=76281980&t=588)** The mobile geodatabase is built upon open source SQLite which means it has the advantages of being viewable by third party SQL software, being open source so that there's no licensing concerns, and with global use of SQLite as the preferred mobile app database engine, the mobile geodatabase has become Esri's recommended choice for geodatabase types.

#### Mastering raster GIS data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Mastering raster GIS data fundamentals will enable advanced analysis and cartography.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=7)** And unlike complicated vector data structures, the raster data model has a simple and elegant structure.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=13)** To begin, I want to show you the kinds of raster data supported in ArcGIS and ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=20)** So let's do a quick internet search with Esri's great help feature.

>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=35)** I'm going to use Esri's internet help now with ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=41)** Okay, I've done a search for ArcGIS Pro Help, and here I am.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=45)** And now I'll copy in that term raster file formats and do a search.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=52)** And we'll choose raster file formats.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=56)** So here on this page are the vast number of raster data file formats that ArcGIS Pro can read in.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=65)** And many of these are also available in ArcGIS.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=70)** You can see this page is very, very extensive.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=73)** So there are many kinds of raster data file formats that are available to us within ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=82)** Now let's discuss the different elements of the raster data model itself.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=87)** The raster data model is elegant, and although there are many different file extensions, there is a common file structure across those extensions.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=97)** First, raster data has a grid system of rows and columns and within those rows and columns we have cells or pixels, and each pixel has a single digital number.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=109)** It could be an integer or it could be a decimal number such as a floating point number.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=114)** A raster can also be geo-referenced and some rasters have multiple bands.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=120)** This is especially the case when we have spectral imagery.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=125)** There is a considerable amount of raster data available and different types of raster data can be grouped into categories.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=132)** We have satellite imagery, and we've already explored that with Earth Explorer.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=138)** We also have digital elevation models and digital orthophoto quads.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=144)** We have digital raster graphics, which are rasterized versions of toposheets.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=149)** And finally, imagery or graphics that are scanned files are raster data.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=155)** Now let's open up ArcGIS Pro and explore the raster data model together.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=161)** Here we are in ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=164)** In the exercise file folder you can open up the basin_bb raster.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=170)** I'll go ahead and grab that now from catalog under the Raster_DEM folder and the_basin_bb.

> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=179)** This raster is a digital elevation model in Big Bend, Texas, which I downloaded from the Texas GIS government website.

> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-raster-gis-data?u=76281980&t=188)** In the contents here you can see the values showing the elevation from high to low.

> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/solution-vectorization-vs-rasterization?u=76281980&t=109)** In this case, this particular layer is unprojected.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/solution-vectorization-vs-rasterization?u=76281980&t=113)** It's just geographic coordinates, and so this latitude and longitude coordinate information isn't very meaningful to me, but in my analysis, what I'm most interested in is just the lineup of the raster and the vector before I would convert them into projected layers to actually do an analysis of their areas.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/solution-vectorization-vs-rasterization?u=76281980&t=135)** Okay, the polygon to raster is complete.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/solution-vectorization-vs-rasterization?u=76281980&t=139)** Now, let's go ahead and take a look by zooming in to check our results and it looks like there is some discrepancy.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/solution-vectorization-vs-rasterization?u=76281980&t=147)** Right here, you can see that the raster layer actually extends beyond the polygon layer, and so if we follow the line, we can see some other areas where the overlap isn't precise and so when we're converting from vector to raster or raster to vector, we need to again be aware of these possibilities, so good job.

#### What is a developable surface?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Mastering projections is required in real-world GIS, so let's build your understanding of developable surfaces.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=8)** The concept of a geographic projection involves taking a three-dimensional Earth and putting it on a two-dimensional format, such as a piece of paper or a computer screen, or some-other two dimensional medium.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=22)** Borden Dent in 1999 defines projections as "The systematic arrangement of the Earth's meridians and parallels onto a plane surface."
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=33)** From the previous video where I introduced the concept of a graticule, along with reduction in scale of Earth, we can use a mathematical transformation to put the 3D Earth onto a 2D surface.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=47)** To do this, it is most easily visualized in the form of a developable surface.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=53)** You can think of a developable surface just as a 2D object that you can manipulate by bending or moving.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=59)** Maybe like a piece of paper.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=61)** Although technically 3D, it's basically can function as a 2D object.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=67)** So let's assume two things.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=69)** First, our piece of paper can fit around a globe like this, and secondly, our globe has see-through lines or graticule lines on it.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=80)** Now if we wrap the paper around the see-through globe at the equator in the form of a cylinder where it touches only the equator, and we put a light source inside our globe, we would see the graticule lines projected onto the paper.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=98)** And if we could imprint those lines onto the paper permanently, and then unroll the cylinder and place it on a table, where it was flat, we could say we've just created a cylindrical projection of the Earth.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=112)** The scale of the globe will be the same on the paper, but only precisely the same where the paper touched the globe, in this case, at the equator.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=122)** So in this example, we would say that scale is true along the equator, and is distorted away from that line at zero degrees latitude.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=133)** There are three main developable surfaces, the cylinder, the cone, and the plane, or the as azimuthal surface.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=141)** The shapes of these kinds of surfaces produce projections linked to their name.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=146)** Thus, we have cylindrical projections, conic projections, and azimuthal projections.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=152)** We can move the developable surface around the globe too, to produce different forms or projections.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=159)** The transverse projection or the oblique angle projection are examples.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=164)** Now, wherever the developable surface touches the globe, it is tangent to the globe, so we call that the standard line, and that's where scale is true.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=174)** We could also create two standard lines if we made our developable surface cut right through the globe itself.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=182)** In this example, notice the cone is actually cutting through the Earth at two spots.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=188)** We call this case the secant case instead of the tangent case.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=193)** The secant case is when there are two lines of scale that are true.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=198)** Whenever we create a projection away from the standard line or lines, there is distortion.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-a-developable-surface?u=76281980&t=205)** In the last video of this section, I will cover distortion, and I will show you different projections with the Tissot's indicatrix circles.

#### Using geoids, spheroids, and datums in GIS
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Now let's explore the concepts of Geoids, Spheroids, and Datums.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=6)** The earth is irregular in shape because of its rotation and its geology, so it has undulations and irregularity, even though it's round in shape.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=16)** Geodetic scientists have tried to model the surface of the earth and they have created the geoid, which is an irregular oval or egg-shaped surface that tries to approximate the surface of the Earth.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=29)** The geoid, offers a nice, smoother surface to work with when trying to model the earth, especially in a computerized environment, but because the geoid is also an irregular shape it's difficult to use in a mathematical sense for modeling earth.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=46)** Therefore, geodetic scientists have used the ellipsoid to approximate the geoid, so the ellipsoid approximates the geoid, which approximates the surface of the Earth.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=58)** The ellipsoid is a very easy model to use, to model the curvature of the Earth and this can be done easily using the concept of the semi major axis and the semi minor axis.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=72)** If we adjust either one of these axes, then earth is adjusted and we can then model the earth and its curvature to try and determine the real distances between places, especially over large geographies like continents.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=88)** The model of Earth we choose to model a particular location then becomes very important.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=94)** We can adjust the semi major and semi minor axes to change the curvature.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=100)** What this means is that different countries around the world choose different ellipsoids to map their locations because it best represents the curvature of the Earth at their location.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=113)** In addition to this concept of the ellipsoid we have the datum.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=117)** Datums are simply a reference system of points, systematically put onto an ellipsoid.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=124)** Essentially, you can think of this as a series of points that are interconnected or maybe form triangles.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=132)** An example of this can be seen from my travels at the Hoover Dam.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=136)** Here I found the USGS datum marker on the Hoover Dam.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=140)** This benchmark location serves as a reference location for surveys.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=145)** Often locations and elevations are reported on these kinds of markers.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=151)** Now, some significant datums have been created in the United States.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=155)** The 1927 North American Datum, or NAD27 is an example.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=161)** This particular datum uses the Clark 1866 ellipsoid, and this is a convenient way to describe a semi-major and semi-minor axis, often ellipsoids are attributed to a person who created them, or the location that best describes where they were created.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=178)** Using benchmarks across the United States like the one I showed you at the Hoover Dam, but starting in Manhattan, Kansas the United States was measured in terms of distance to those benchmarks and their elevations.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=192)** In a moment, we'll see these measurements didn't quite get as precise as we'd like.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=197)** Now, an updated version of NAD27 is NAD83, the North American Datum of 1983, and that utilized satellite technology.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=208)** In this case, the GRS80 spheroid was used, and here are the particulars about the semi major and semi minor axis for that particular ellipsoid.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=218)** And it's not so important to know these particular distances from a GIS practitioner standpoint, but it is important to know that the semi major and semi minor axis can be adjusted, which then results in the adjustment of the curvature of the earth of the model of your geography, in this case, the North American continent.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=239)** The last common datum that I'd like to talk about is the WGS84 or World Geodetic System of 1984.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=248)** In this case, the GRS80 spheroid is adjusted very, very slightly, which results in a nice global sphere or ellipsoid that is used on almost every GPS handheld device or receiver and smartphone.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=265)** Also, the coordinate system of latitude and longitude that you find on your most popular mapping applications often are reported using the particular WGS84 ellipsoid.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=276)** If you were to choose a different datum such as NAD27, and you reported latitude and longitude for NAD27, those locations would be different than they would be reported for WGS84 because it's a different model of the earth.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=295)** Now, to get an idea how this datum shift occurs, let's look at the NAD27 compared to the NAD83 results.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=304)** Notice here near the center of the United States, the accuracy is pretty good comparing these two, but as we extend to the coast, to the west and to the east the datum shift between 27 and 83 is pretty significant where in some places we're well over 100 meters off.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=322)** With the advancement in satellite technology, we've been able to increase our accuracy and precision of coordinate location.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/using-geoids-spheroids-and-datums-in-gis?u=76281980&t=329)** So now that we've explored the graticule, the developable surface, geoids, spheroids, and datums, let's go ahead and take a look at all of these things together using the Indicatric circles.

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In previous videos I've shown you the graticule scale or reduction of earth, developable surfaces, ellipsoids, geoids and datums.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=9)** So now let's master projections in GIS.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=14)** First, it's important to consider that when we go from 3D Earth to a 2D medium we have distortion.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=21)** Projections help us compensate for distortion by allowing us to preserve some element.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=27)** For example, equivalent projections preserve areas.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=32)** So if you're mapping a map of population density, you'll want to preserve your area because you're looking at people per area.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=41)** An equivalent projection would be a good choice.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=44)** Another option would be a conformal projection, which preserves angles.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=49)** When you preserve angles, a byproduct is that the shape of things is preserved.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=54)** We'll talk about that in just a minute.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=56)** Another category to consider is the compromise projection.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=60)** Although it doesn't preserve area or angle, it tries to minimize distortion overall.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=66)** And usually our global projections are compromised projections.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=71)** There are two other aspects that we might preserve, such as direction and distance.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=75)** However, maps that preserve angles cannot preserve areas and maps that preserve areas cannot preserve angles.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=83)** So we have to choose either an equivalent, conformal or some other type of projection.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=90)** So what does it mean to preserve angles in a map projection?
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=94)** Well, let's start here with our longitude lines.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=97)** In this case, I have 48 degrees and 49 degrees respectively.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=101)** Now, if we draw a line across these two longitude lines, such as this, and we measure the angles such as A and B and then we find that A equals B, that means that our vector or our rhumb line or loxodrome is consistent across the lines of longitude.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=125)** And if this is the case, then the angle is preserved and the byproduct is that the shape of things will be preserved in our map, so we have a conformal map.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=138)** One of the best ways that we can understand this idea of distortion is through the use of Tissot's indicatrix circles.

> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=146)** The symbol representing a point on a reference globe with a unit radius is called a Tissot's indicatrix.

> **[8:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=513)** Let's take a look at another one.
>
> **[8:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=515)** Here I'm going to choose properties and in this case let's look at oh, Goode's world atlas views.
>
> **[8:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=524)** So Goode's homolosine land view.
>
> **[8:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=527)** So here it's kind of the orange peel idea of a projection.
>
> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=531)** Again, another compromise projection.
>
> **[8:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=534)** That's pretty powerful, right?
>
> **[8:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=536)** We don't have a big adjustment in the size of the Tissot's indicatrix circles in terms of their shape and their size but a very nice compromise overall, a beautiful projection.
>
> **[9:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=549)** Now let's take a look at Mercator's projection.
>
> **[9:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=552)** So we'll go here and we will scroll down to the Mercator projection, the infamous Mercator projection that many of you are familiar with.
>
> **[9:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=561)** Okay, here we go.
>
> **[9:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=563)** So the famous Mercator projection is a conformal projection.
>
> **[9:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=568)** In this case, angle is preserved, the shape of things is preserved, but area is exaggerated dramatically especially to the north and the south.
>
> **[9:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=579)** Of course, Greenland in real life is not nearly as big as the southern cone of South America, but in the Mercator projection, Greenland appears huge because it's near the poles.
>
> **[9:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=592)** And also take a look at Antarctica.
>
> **[9:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=594)** It looks like it's a giant land mass, when in fact it's much, much smaller than this.
>
> **[10:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=601)** And let's go ahead and choose one last projection to take a look at.
>
> **[10:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=606)** Let's choose the Robinson projection, after Doctor Arthur Robinson.
>
> **[10:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=611)** Okay, so this is a wonderful global projection that is a compromise projection.
>
> **[10:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=618)** Here you can see a global picture where distortion is kept at a minimum with the view of these Tissot indicatrix circles.
>
> **[10:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=627)** So all of these adjustments have been on the fly.
>
> **[10:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=631)** We haven't made any permanent adjustment to the Tissot's indicatrix circles.
>
> **[10:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=637)** So that brings me to this concept of what happens if we put another layer into the contents pane that we have here.
>
> **[10:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=646)** What should happen is that the layer on the fly will adjust to whatever projection we have.
>
> **[10:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=653)** Here we have the Robinson projection and I'll add a new layer, the state of Michigan block groups that we grabbed and downloaded from the Census Bureau earlier in this course.
>
> **[11:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=664)** So here I'll add data and I will choose to add those block groups. There we go.
>
> **[11:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=672)** And they were added right here, the state of Michigan.
>
> **[11:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=675)** And look it conformed exactly right at the angle there of the Robinson projection based on where it is in the world.
>
> **[11:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=684)** It will conform on the fly.
>
> **[11:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=687)** But to permanently change a map projection from one projection to another, you'll need to use the toolbox.
>
> **[11:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=696)** So let me show you that now.
>
> **[11:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=697)** Here under tools and geoprocessing, we click on toolboxes and we can go down to data management tools, projections and transformations and then we can actually project one layer from one kind of projection into another kind of projection permanently.
>
> **[11:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=718)** So if you're doing real world GIS, that means that you should be putting your layers into the same projection if you're conducting an analysis.
>
> **[12:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/mastering-projections-in-gis?u=76281980&t=727)** So let's do a challenge around that idea.

### 4. How to Collect GIS Data in the Field?

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Geospatial data collection basics
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] When we consider the challenges associated with the geospatial data collection process, there are a few things you need to plan for to successfully complete your project.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=11)** Time and cost are variables that we're most interested in and they have sub components.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=17)** So let's break down each and dive deeper.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=21)** In the planning process, time is one of the key considerations, and you can think of time as not only including the total amount of time it takes to complete the data collection, but also the cost in person hours to collect it.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=35)** Time takes on a variety of forms because of the interconnectedness of time to machines via persons.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=42)** And although it's difficult to plan for, the malfunction of machines and the data collection process always increases the total time, and it happens to me all the time.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=52)** Planning for computer failures, GPS issues required software updates, IT schedules for maintenance and personnel schedules, they all play a key fixture in the total time calculation.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=65)** For my projects, I usually build in a 15% buffer into the total time needed to complete a project based on these variables that are often difficult to assess.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=76)** Now, for longer projects that take more than two or three weeks, that only include a handful of people or maybe just myself, I usually will call my IT department to see what updates they are planning, especially for the hardware updates that are coming.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=92)** Now, cost is the other variable to consider in the planning process.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=97)** Usually cost is associated with person hours paid in the collection process, but it also includes the hardware and the software costs, especially those that might need upgraded or purchased.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=111)** And certainly I recommend knowing the data collectors and their skills if the project involves complicated data collection, especially if high levels of accuracy is essential to the output data.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=123)** Now, if it's not possible to know them, then it's key to train the most skillful of your team members to transfer the instructions to the data collectors, and skilled transfer translates to cost, and as you know, the more skilled the data collectors are the more you'll be paying them to do the work.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/geospatial-data-collection-basics?u=76281980&t=141)** Therefore, when creating cost benefit analysis, I'm a little more conservative when it comes to the calculated cost and I usually include a 3% to even sometimes 5% extra cost buffer so that I'm able to give a more realistic estimate of the final cost.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (1), for, (1)
> **Env Vars:** gps (1)
> **Speakers:** - [narrator] (1)

#### How to create a spatial database from coordinates
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-create-a-spatial-database-from-coordinates?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-create-a-spatial-database-from-coordinates?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the easiest ways to collect geospatial data, is from the world of online maps.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-create-a-spatial-database-from-coordinates?u=76281980&t=6)** Let me show you two examples, first, with Google and then with online base maps, from Esri inside of ArcGIS Pro.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-create-a-spatial-database-from-coordinates?u=76281980&t=16)** So here we are in Google Maps, and let's build a geospatial database together.
>

#### How to collect GIS data using ArcGIS Survey123
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the most exciting software products developed by Esri is Survey123.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=6)** This software is a powerful tool for collecting data in the field, but what is more powerful are the tools that let you build a survey instrument before you send your teams out to collect the data.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=18)** I want to show you how to use it for data collection and mapping.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=22)** Survey123 is an online Esri site where you can construct a survey for data collection.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=28)** So, if the job requires you to collect data in the field, you can design what Esri calls a survey instrument on your computer.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=37)** You set all the parameters for the data collection process like a map and all the fields for attributes of the things that you're collecting.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=45)** For those using Trimble GPS devices and software, it's like a data dictionary concept.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=52)** You have to have a smart device and download the Survey123 app onto it.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=57)** And once you've done that, you log into Survey123 on your smart device app, download the survey instrument you created on your computer, and then you can start collecting data in the field with it.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=68)** It's awesome.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=70)** Since the smart device has a GPS receiver on it, you can get location data usually within about three meters accuracy.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-to-collect-gis-data-using-arcgis-survey123?u=76281980&t=78)** Now, if you need higher precision accuracy then you'll need to use formal high precision GPS or total station instruments, which may or may not be able to use Survey123.
>

### 5. How to Master ArcGIS Online?

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### What is ArcGIS Online?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Jason] ArcGIS Online is an environment that allows you to map, store, and distribute spatial data, as well as build compelling computer web mapping applications.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=11)** Here we are at [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com).
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=14)** There is a subscription-based [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) that allows you to develop ArcGIS server like map services and geoprocessing applications as well as access premium served data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=27)** Now, the subscription-based license approach is run through an organizational account, but companies can also install it on a local intranet and host it internally.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=37)** If that's the case, it's called ArcGIS portal.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=41)** Now, let's go ahead and sign in to [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) and explore this environment together.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-is-arcgis-online?u=76281980&t=47)** In the upper right, you can choose to sign in and what we're going to do is use my public account to see all the things that are possible.
>

### 7. How to Land a GIS job?

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### What are the different types of GIS jobs?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So what are the kinds of GIS jobs out there?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=4)** Well, we can typically organize GIS positions as either an analyst position, developer or database manager, and, of course, all of these areas will overlap with one another.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=17)** When looking for GIS jobs, usually the advertisement specifies the expectations linked to one of these three, and although it's good to have experience in all three, getting depth in one will really help you gain greater potential toward job promotion.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=33)** Most GIS graduate programs will prepare you well in all of these areas.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=38)** Sometimes employers do not know exactly what they need and so it's important to be able to describe back to them in both their terms and your terms what you can offer them with your level of GIS expertise.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=51)** You might not consider yourself an expert, but it is likely that you do have expert knowledge in GIS, especially if you've gone through this course.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=59)** Now, let's take a look together at these positions and I want you to think about where you are in this model.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=66)** The analyst position typically is one where GIS experts are using GIS to analyze landscape, demographics or maybe spatially located phenomena for business purposes.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=78)** You can think of it as doing the science of GIS.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=81)** For example, land suitability analysis is typically GIS analyst procedures for businesses to make decisions on where to put their next location.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=91)** For example, if we had a fictitious business, let's call it make a lot of pants, and they were collecting zip codes from their customers during a three week span at the checkout aisle, which allowed them to collect geospatial locations of all their customers, then they could use that knowledge and build a social and demographic analysis combining average household size with maybe census data to analyze where all of their customers were living and build an entire social and demographic profile of their whole customer base and then they would use that to place their next door.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=128)** Of course, market analysis like this is much more sophisticated, but it does give you an example of what an analyst would do.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=136)** As a GIS developer, the business expectations from the employer is not only that you will provide analysis, but that you'll also develop applications that allow users, internal and external to the company, to have the ability to visualize and analyze data on a map interface.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=155)** If you're currently in school working on GIS or looking to change jobs into GIS, building applications is the easiest way to demonstrate your skills.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=165)** You will also be called on to develop GIS Workflows that others can use, whether it's a GIS modeling workflow where you have to develop step-by-step procedures about GIS inputs to give a specific kind of GIS output or perhaps the development of a more sophisticated cardiographic product such as an Atlas series or a set of base maps for your business, GIS Workflow development is likely to be an expectation.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=194)** In this course, I've shown you how to build compelling web maps and then how to deploy web mapping applications.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=200)** You've also learned how to access GIS data from a variety of places, pull it into your software and make it ready for mapping.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=208)** As you develop your GIS skills more, you'll continue to develop new and richer GIS Workflows.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=215)** Finally, the database manager position best describes your abilities to handle data and server details.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=222)** Positions in this type of GIS job require deeper IT and CS development, and often they are considered positions in data stewardship.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=232)** In my experience thus far, many of these positions are held by students with degrees in geography or and computer science, and sometimes those computer scientists have learned just some GIS.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=245)** However, the more powerful scenario is someone who's able to do both deeply.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=249)** Many data science majors take GIS with me and I also have computer science faculty teaching directly in my GIS program at the university.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=259)** After all, geographic information systems is a subset of information system technology so there is a great potential for exchange between computer scientists and geographers like myself.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=270)** Focusing training usually in a geography department while at the university, is likely to allow you the greatest flexibility in employment but more it will give you the ability to expertly supervise the whole process of GIS development, analysis and maintenance.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=287)** Usually, my students are strongest in the areas having a solid understanding of programming and Python coding, and in our studio for statistical analysis.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=298)** This training becomes even more important for those wanting to do development work using GIS servers.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=304)** It is important to know that some job requirements exclude you because of lack of experience.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=309)** However, most employers will recognize paid internships and years in graduate school as time of experience.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=317)** Whatever your GIS interests, it's important that you're able to document your experiences on a resume and bring knowledge and enthusiasm to the interview.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/what-are-the-different-types-of-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=325)** The best words of wisdom I can impart is to prepare, prepare and prepare some more before you interview.

#### Where can you find GIS jobs?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-can-you-find-gis-jobs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-can-you-find-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now, let's talk about jobs.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-can-you-find-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=2)** Of course, you're thinking about searches locally for GIS jobs but don't discount the place that you might want to be too because I always encourage my students that they'll find a larger number of jobs if they're willing to be mobile or to work remotely.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/where-can-you-find-gis-jobs?u=76281980&t=19)** Now, if you're interested in local or regional public government GIS positions, these are only usually advertised on local government websites so you'd have to do a search with that approach.

>

>

>

>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-can-you-master-the-gis-job-interview-part-1?u=76281980&t=78)** So think about what that might be for you.

>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-can-you-master-the-gis-job-interview-part-1?u=76281980&t=89)** Everyone is telling me that companies want proven people who can work in groups, so give some extra time to preparation of this question.

>

>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-can-you-master-the-gis-job-interview-part-1?u=76281980&t=102)** Try to think about how your weaknesses might be turned into strengths.
>

>

>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/real-world-gis-22715766/how-can-you-master-the-gis-job-interview-part-1?u=76281980&t=124)** That is a great way to approach your weaknesses and strengths.

>
